id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>\n<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<table class="external text" href="http://un.org/ga" rel="nofollow">un<wbr/>.org<wbr/>/ga</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Membership and participation\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>\n<p>For two articles dealing with membership of and participation in the General Assembly, see:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">General Assembly members</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">General Assembly observers</a></li></ul>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>United Nations General Assembly</b> (<b>UNGA</b> or  <b>GA</b>; French: <i lang="fr">Assembl&#233;e G&#233;n&#233;rale</i>, AG) is one of the six principal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organs_of_the_United_Nations" title="Organs of the United Nations">organs of the</a> United Nations (UN), the only one in which all member nations have equal representation, and the main deliberative, policy-making, and representative organ of the UN. Its powers are to oversee the budget of the UN, appoint the non-permanent members to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a>, appoint the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General of the United Nations</a>, receive reports from other parts of the UN, and make recommendations in the form of <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_resolution" title="United Nations General Assembly resolution">General Assembly Resolutions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> It has also established numerous <a href="/wiki/Category:United_Nations_General_Assembly_subsidiary_organs" title="Category:United Nations General Assembly subsidiary organs">subsidiary organs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The General Assembly currently meets under <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="President of the United Nations General Assembly">its president</a> or <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">secretary-general</a> in annual sessions at the <a href="/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations" title="Headquarters of the United Nations">headquarters of the United Nations</a> in New York City, the main part of which lasts from September<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> to December and part of January until all issues are addressed (which often is just before the next session\'s start). It can also reconvene for special and emergency special sessions. Its composition, functions, powers, voting, and procedures are set out in <a href="/wiki/Chapter_IV_of_the_United_Nations_Charter" title="Chapter IV of the United Nations Charter">Chapter IV of the United Nations Charter</a>. The first session was convened on 10 January 1946 in the <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Central_Hall,_Westminster" title="Methodist Central Hall, Westminster">Methodist Central Hall</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and included representatives of 51 nations.\n</p><p>Voting in the General Assembly on certain important questions, namely, recommendations on peace and security, budgetary concerns, and the election, admission, suspension or expulsion of members is by a <a href="/wiki/Supermajority" title="Supermajority">two-thirds majority</a> of those present and voting. Other questions are decided by a straightforward <a href="/wiki/Majority" title="Majority">majority</a>. Each member country has one vote. Apart from approval of budgetary matters, including adoption of a scale of assessment, Assembly resolutions are not binding on the members. The Assembly may make recommendations on any matters within the scope of the UN, except matters of peace and security under Security Council consideration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-4">[4]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Representation_(politics)" title="Representation (politics)">one state, one vote</a> power structure potentially allows states comprising just five percent of the world population to pass a resolution by a two-thirds vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-population-5">[5]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 1980s, the Assembly became a forum for the "North-South dialogue": the discussion of issues between industrialized nations and developing countries. These issues came to the fore because of the phenomenal growth and changing makeup of the UN membership. In 1945, the UN had 51 members. It now has 193, of which more than two-thirds are <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a>. Because of their numbers, developing countries are often able to determine the agenda of the Assembly (using coordinating groups like the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_77" title="Group of 77">G77</a>), the character of its debates, and the nature of its decisions. For many developing countries, the UN is the source of much of their diplomatic influence and the principal outlet for their foreign relations initiatives.\n</p><p>Although the resolutions passed by the General Assembly do not have the binding forces over the member nations (apart from budgetary measures), pursuant to its <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_377" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 377">Uniting for Peace</a> resolution of November 1950 (resolution 377 (V)), the Assembly may also take action if the Security Council fails to act, owing to the negative vote of a <a href="/wiki/Permanent_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="Permanent members of the United Nations Security Council">permanent member</a>, in a case where there appears to be a threat to the peace, breach of the peace or act of aggression. The Assembly can consider the matter immediately with a view to making recommendations to Members for collective measures to maintain or restore international peace and security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-4">[4]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Methodist.central.hall.london.arp.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1413" data-file-width="1656" decoding="async" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Methodist.central.hall.london.arp.jpg/220px-Methodist.central.hall.london.arp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Methodist.central.hall.london.arp.jpg/330px-Methodist.central.hall.london.arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Methodist.central.hall.london.arp.jpg/440px-Methodist.central.hall.london.arp.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Methodist.central.hall.london.arp.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Methodist_Central_Hall,_Westminster" title="Methodist Central Hall, Westminster">Methodist Central Hall</a>, London, the location of the first meeting of the United Nations General Assembly in 1946.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The first session of the UN General Assembly was convened on 10 January 1946 in the Methodist Central Hall in London and included representatives of 51 nations. The next few annual sessions were held in different cities: the second session in New York City, and the third in Paris. It moved to the permanent <a href="/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations" title="Headquarters of the United Nations">Headquarters of the United Nations</a> in New York City at the start of its seventh regular annual session, on 14 October 1952. In December 1988, in order to hear <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a>, the General Assembly organized its 29th session in the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Nations" title="Palace of Nations">Palace of Nations</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>, Switzerland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership">Membership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Membership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">Member states of the United Nations</a></div>\n<p>All 193 members of the United Nations are members of the General Assembly, with the addition of Holy See and Palestine as observer states. Further, the United Nations General Assembly may grant <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">observer status</a> to an international organization or entity, which entitles the entity to participate in the work of the United Nations General Assembly, though with limitations.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Agenda">Agenda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Agenda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The agenda for each session is planned up to seven months in advance and begins with the release of a preliminary list of items to be included in the provisional agenda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> This is refined into a provisional agenda 60 days before the opening of the session. After the session begins, the final agenda is adopted in a plenary meeting which allocates the work to the various Main Committees, who later submit reports back to the Assembly for adoption by consensus or by vote.\n</p><p>Items on the agenda are numbered. Regular plenary sessions of the General Assembly in recent years have initially been scheduled to be held over the course of just three months; however, additional work loads have extended these sessions until just short of the next session. The routinely scheduled portions of the sessions normally commence on "the Tuesday of the third week in September, counting from the first week that contains at least one working day", per the UN Rules of Procedure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The last two of these Regular sessions were routinely scheduled to recess exactly three months afterwards<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> in early December, but were resumed in January and extended until just before the beginning of the following sessions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Resolutions">Resolutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Resolutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-Refimprove_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_resolution" title="United Nations General Assembly resolution">United Nations General Assembly resolution</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Document_Codes" title="United Nations Document Codes">United Nations Document Codes</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_in_the_United_States_24_September_2009-5.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="434" data-file-width="650" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Dmitry_Medvedev_in_the_United_States_24_September_2009-5.jpg/220px-Dmitry_Medvedev_in_the_United_States_24_September_2009-5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Dmitry_Medvedev_in_the_United_States_24_September_2009-5.jpg/330px-Dmitry_Medvedev_in_the_United_States_24_September_2009-5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Dmitry_Medvedev_in_the_United_States_24_September_2009-5.jpg/440px-Dmitry_Medvedev_in_the_United_States_24_September_2009-5.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_in_the_United_States_24_September_2009-5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Russian President <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a> addresses the 64th session of the UN General Assembly on 24 September 2009</div></div></div>\n<p>The General Assembly votes on many resolutions brought forth by sponsoring states. These are generally statements symbolizing the sense of the international community about an array of world issues. Most General Assembly resolutions are not enforceable as a legal or practical matter, because the General Assembly lacks enforcement powers with respect to most issues. The General Assembly has authority to make final decisions in some areas such as the United Nations budget.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p><p>General Assembly Resolutions are generally non-binding on member states, but carry considerable political weight, and are legally binding towards the operations of the General Assembly. The General Assembly can also refer an issue to the Security Council to put in place a binding resolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Resolution_numbering_scheme">Resolution numbering scheme</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Resolution numbering scheme">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>From the First to the Thirtieth General Assembly sessions, all General Assembly resolutions were numbered consecutively, with the resolution number followed by the session number in Roman numbers (for example, <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_1514" title="s:United Nations General Assembly Resolution 1514">Resolution 1514 (XV)</a>, which was the 1514th numbered resolution adopted by the Assembly, and was adopted at the Fifteenth Regular Session (1960)). Beginning in the Thirty-First Session, resolutions are numbered by individual session (for example Resolution 41/10 represents the 10th resolution adopted at the Forty-First Session).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="UNGA_budget">UNGA budget</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: UNGA budget">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The General Assembly also approves the budget of the United Nations and decides how much money each member state must pay to run the organization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-population-5">[5]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Charter of the United Nations gives responsibility for approving the budget to the General Assembly (Chapter IV, Article 17) and for preparing the budget to the Secretary-General, as "chief administrative officer" (Chapter XV, Article 97). The Charter also addresses the non-payment of assessed contributions (Chapter IV, Article 19).\nThe planning, programming, budgeting, monitoring and evaluation cycle of the United Nations has evolved over the years; major resolutions on the process include General Assembly resolutions: 41/213 of 19 December 1986, 42/211 of 21 December 1987, and 45/248 of 21 December 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The budget covers the costs of United Nations programmes in areas such as political affairs, international justice and law, international cooperation for development, public information, human rights, and humanitarian affairs.\n</p><p>The main source of funds for the regular budget is the contributions of member states. The scale of assessments is based on the capacity of countries to pay. This is determined by considering their relative shares of total gross national product, adjusted to take into account a number of factors, including their per capita incomes.\n</p><p>In addition to the regular budget, member states are assessed for the costs of the international tribunals and, in accordance with a modified version of the basic scale, for the costs of peacekeeping operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:United_National_General_Assembly.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="185" data-file-width="360" decoding="async" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/United_National_General_Assembly.svg/220px-United_National_General_Assembly.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/United_National_General_Assembly.svg/330px-United_National_General_Assembly.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/United_National_General_Assembly.svg/440px-United_National_General_Assembly.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:United_National_General_Assembly.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Division of the General Assembly by membership in the five <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Regional_Groups" title="United Nations Regional Groups">United Nations Regional Groups</a>. <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0000ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;The African Group</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #339900; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;The Asia-Pacific Group</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #cc0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160; The Middle and Eastern European Group</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #cc3399; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;The Latin American and Caribbean States (GRULAC)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #cc9900; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;The Western European and Others Group (WEOG)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #708090; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;No group</div></div></div></div>\n<p>The General Assembly votes in elections for the ten non-permanent members of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> the most recent such election was on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_election,_2017" title="United Nations Security Council election, 2017">2 June 2017</a>. These elections take place every year, and member states serve two-year terms, with five replaced each year. The candidates are selected by their <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Regional_Groups" title="United Nations Regional Groups">regional groups</a>. The General Assembly also elects members of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council" title="United Nations Economic and Social Council">United Nations Economic and Social Council</a>. It also elects members of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Industrial_Development_Organization" title="United Nations Industrial Development Organization">United Nations Industrial Development Organization</a>, and some members of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Trusteeship_Council" title="United Nations Trusteeship Council">United Nations Trusteeship Council</a>. The General Assembly appoints the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General of the United Nations</a> on recommendation of the Security Council, and adopts rules governing the administration of the Secretariat. Along with the Security Council, the General Assembly elects Judges for the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Special_sessions_.28UNGASS.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_sessions_(UNGASS)">Special sessions (UNGASS)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Special sessions (UNGASS)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:General_Assembly_of_the_United_Nations.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/General_Assembly_of_the_United_Nations.jpg/220px-General_Assembly_of_the_United_Nations.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/General_Assembly_of_the_United_Nations.jpg/330px-General_Assembly_of_the_United_Nations.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/General_Assembly_of_the_United_Nations.jpg/440px-General_Assembly_of_the_United_Nations.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:General_Assembly_of_the_United_Nations.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spanish Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero" title="Jos&#233; Luis Rodr&#237;guez Zapatero">Jos&#233; Luis Rodr&#237;guez Zapatero</a> addressing the General Assembly in New York, 20 September 2005</div></div></div>\n<p>Special sessions may be convened at the request of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>, or a majority of UN members,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> or, if the majority concurs, of a single member. A special session was held on October 1995 at the head of government level to commemorate the UN\'s 50th anniversary. Another special session was held in September 2000 to celebrate the millennium; it put forward the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a>. A special session was again held to discuss and admit proposals for the <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> crisis in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> A further special session (<a href="/wiki/2005_World_Summit" title="2005 World Summit">2005 World Summit</a>) was held in September 2005 to commemorate the UN\'s 60th anniversary; it assessed progress on the Millennium Development Goals, and discussed <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a>\'s <i>In Larger Freedom</i> proposals. Another special session was held in 2014 to discuss Population and Development, following the International Conference on Population and Development Programme of Action.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UNGASS_2016">UNGASS 2016</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: UNGASS 2016">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A special session was held in 2016 to discuss the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_on_Drugs" title="War on Drugs">War on Drugs</a> and proposals to reconsider international drug treaties like the <a href="/wiki/Single_Convention_on_Narcotic_Drugs" title="Single Convention on Narcotic Drugs">Single Convention on Narcotic Drugs</a>, as well as how to deal with drug treatment, rehabilitation, and related matters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> This was the first UN gathering on the subject in 20 years. In 2016, while "some European and South American countries as well as the U.S. favored softer approaches[,] ... countries such as China and Russia and most Muslim nations like Iran, Indonesia and Pakistan remained staunchly opposed" to any move beyond prohibition. One group favouring reform, the <a href="/wiki/Global_Commission_on_Drug_Policy" title="Global Commission on Drug Policy">Global Commission on Drug Policy</a>, and some attendees, <a href="/wiki/Global_Commission_on_Drug_Policy#Disappointment_with_UNGASS_2016" title="Global Commission on Drug Policy">expressed disappointment</a> with the "status quo" outcome.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Presenters included <a href="/wiki/Russel_Simmons" title="Russel Simmons">Russel Simmons</a>, Michael Skolnik, <a href="/wiki/Rhymefest" title="Rhymefest">Che Rhymefest Smith</a>, who screened the film WARonUS, directed by <a href="/wiki/Queen_Muhammad_Ali" title="Queen Muhammad Ali">Queen Muhammad Ali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hakeem_Khaaliq" title="Hakeem Khaaliq">Hakeem Khaaliq</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rousseff_UN_General_Debate.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1169" data-file-width="1753" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Rousseff_UN_General_Debate.jpg/220px-Rousseff_UN_General_Debate.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Rousseff_UN_General_Debate.jpg/330px-Rousseff_UN_General_Debate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Rousseff_UN_General_Debate.jpg/440px-Rousseff_UN_General_Debate.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rousseff_UN_General_Debate.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Brazilian President <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">Dilma Rousseff</a> delivers the opening speech at the 66th Session of the General Assembly on 21 September 2011, marking the first time a woman opened a United Nations session.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_special_sessions">Other special sessions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Other special sessions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>At the first Special Session of the UN General Assembly held in 1947, <a href="/wiki/Osvaldo_Aranha" title="Osvaldo Aranha">Osvaldo Aranha</a>, then president of the Special Session, began a tradition that has remained until today whereby the first speaker at this major international forum is always a Brazilian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>\n</p><p>If the Security Council fails to act to maintain international peace and security due to a disagreement between its permanent members, the General Assembly has the power to convene an emergency special session and act to ensure peace and security under <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_377" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 377">United Nations General Assembly Resolution 377</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General_Debates">General Debates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: General Debates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Annually, Heads of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Head_of_State" title="Head of State">State</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Head_of_Government" title="Head of Government">Government</a> or heads of delegations speak at the opening of the new session of the General Assembly during the "General Debate".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thailand_2005_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thailand_2005-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Obama_2014_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Obama_2014-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Felipe_VI_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Felipe_VI-29">[29]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Emergency_special_sessions">Emergency special sessions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Emergency special sessions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The General Assembly may take action on maintaining international peace and security if the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> is unable, usually due to disagreement among the permanent members, to exercise its primary responsibility. If not in session at the time, the General Assembly may meet in <a href="/wiki/List_of_emergency_special_sessions_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="List of emergency special sessions of the United Nations General Assembly">emergency special session</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNGAESSs_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNGAESSs-30">[30]</a></sup> within 24 hours of the request. Such emergency special sessions are to be called if requested by the UN Security Council on the vote of any seven members, or by a majority of the Members of the United Nations.\n</p><p>The "<a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_377" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 377">Uniting for Peace</a>" resolution, adopted 3 November 1950, empowered the Assembly to convene in emergency special session in order to recommend collective measures, including the use of armed force, in the event of a breach of the peace or an act of aggression. As with all Assembly resolutions, two-thirds of UN Members "present and voting" must approve any such recommendation before it can be formally adopted by the Assembly. Emergency special sessions have been convened under this procedure on ten occasions. The two most recent, in 1982 and 1997&#8211;2017, were about the status of the territories occupied<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> by the <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">State of Israel</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsidiary_organs">Subsidiary organs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Subsidiary organs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UN_General_Assembly_building.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="659" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/UN_General_Assembly_building.jpg/320px-UN_General_Assembly_building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/UN_General_Assembly_building.jpg/480px-UN_General_Assembly_building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/UN_General_Assembly_building.jpg/640px-UN_General_Assembly_building.jpg 2x" width="320"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UN_General_Assembly_building.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The United Nations General Assembly building</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Panorama_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly,_Oct_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2516" data-file-width="6080" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8e/Panorama_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly%2C_Oct_2012.jpg/320px-Panorama_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly%2C_Oct_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8e/Panorama_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly%2C_Oct_2012.jpg/480px-Panorama_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly%2C_Oct_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8e/Panorama_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly%2C_Oct_2012.jpg/640px-Panorama_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly%2C_Oct_2012.jpg 2x" width="320"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Panorama_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly,_Oct_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Panorama of the UNGA</div></div></div>\n<p>The General Assembly subsidiary organs are divided into five categories: committees (30 total, six main), commissions (six), boards (seven), councils (four) and panels (one), working groups, and "other".\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Committees">Committees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Committees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_committees">Main committees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Main committees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The main committees are <a href="/wiki/Ordinal_number" title="Ordinal number">ordinally numbered</a>, 1&#8211;6:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-main_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-main-32">[32]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>The First Committee: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_First_Committee" title="United Nations General Assembly First Committee">Disarmament and International Security</a> (DISEC) is concerned with disarmament and related international security questions</li>\n<li>The Second Committee: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Second_Committee" title="United Nations General Assembly Second Committee">Economic and Financial</a> (ECOFIN) is concerned with economic questions</li>\n<li>The Third Committee: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Third_Committee" title="United Nations General Assembly Third Committee">Social, Cultural, and Humanitarian</a> (SOCHUM) deals with social and humanitarian issues</li>\n<li>The Fourth Committee: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Fourth_Committee" title="United Nations General Assembly Fourth Committee">Special Political and Decolonisation</a> (SPECPOL) deals with a variety of political subjects not dealt with by the First Committee, as well as with decolonization</li>\n<li>The Fifth Committee: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Fifth_Committee" title="United Nations General Assembly Fifth Committee">Administrative and Budgetary and general</a> deals with the administration and budget of the United Nations</li>\n<li>The Sixth Committee: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Sixth_Committee" title="United Nations General Assembly Sixth Committee">Legal</a> deals with legal matters</li></ul>\n<p>The roles of many of the main committees have changed over time. Until the late 1970s, the First Committee was the Political and Security Committee (POLISEC) and there was also a sufficient number of additional "political" matters that an additional, unnumbered main committee, called the Special Political Committee, also sat. The Fourth Committee formerly handled Trusteeship and Decolonization matters. With the decreasing number of such matters to be addressed as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Trust_Territories" title="United Nations Trust Territories">trust territories</a> attained independence and the <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">decolonization</a> movement progressed, the functions of the Special Political Committee were merged into the Fourth Committee during the 1990s.\n</p><p>Each main committee consists of all the members of the General Assembly. Each elects a chairman, three vice chairmen, and a <a href="/wiki/Rapporteur" title="Rapporteur">rapporteur</a> at the outset of each regular General Assembly session.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_committees">Other committees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Other committees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="695" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg/220px-RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg/330px-RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg/440px-RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_828797_Mikhail_Gorbachev_addressing_UN_General_Assembly_session.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Soviet general secretary <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a> addresses the UN General Assembly in December 1988</div></div></div>\n<p>These are not numbered. According to the General Assembly website, the most important are: <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-main_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-main-32">[32]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_nations_credentials_committee" title="United nations credentials committee">Credentials Committee</a>&#160;&#8211; This committee is charged with ensuring that the <a href="/wiki/Credential#Diplomacy" title="Credential">diplomatic credentials</a> of all UN representatives are in order. The Credentials Committee consists of nine Member States elected early in each regular General Assembly session.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Committee" title="United Nations General Committee">General Committee</a>&#160;&#8211; This is a supervisory committee entrusted with ensuring that the whole meeting of the Assembly goes smoothly. The General Committee consists of the president and vice presidents of the current General Assembly session and the chairman of each of the six Main Committees.</li></ul>\n<p>Other committees of the General Assembly are <a href="/wiki/Enumeration" title="Enumeration">enumerated</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Commissions">Commissions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Commissions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are six commissions: <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Disarmament_Commission" title="United Nations Disarmament Commission">United Nations Disarmament Commission</a>, established by GA Resolution 502 (VI) and S-10/2</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/International_Civil_Service_Commission" title="International Civil Service Commission">International Civil Service Commission</a>, established by GA Resolution 3357 (XXIX)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/International_Law_Commission" title="International Law Commission">International Law Commission</a>, established by GA Resolution 174 (II)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Commission_on_International_Trade_Law" title="United Nations Commission on International Trade Law">United Nations Commission on International Trade Law</a> (UNCITRAL), established by GA Resolution 2205 (XXI)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conciliation_Commission" title="United Nations Conciliation Commission">United Nations Conciliation Commission</a> for Palestine, established by GA Resolution 194 (III)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Peacebuilding_Commission" title="Peacebuilding Commission">United Nations Peacebuilding Commission</a>, established by GA Resolution 60/180 and UN Security Council <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1645" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1645">Resolutions 1645</a> (2005) and 1646 (2005)</li></ul>\n<p>Despite its name, the former <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Commission_on_Human_Rights" title="United Nations Commission on Human Rights">United Nations Commission on Human Rights</a> (UNCHR) was actually a subsidiary body of <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council" title="United Nations Economic and Social Council">ECOSOC</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boards">Boards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Boards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are seven boards which are categorized into two groups:\na) Executive Boards and b) Boards <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive_Boards">Executive Boards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Executive Boards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ol><li>Executive Board of the United Nations Children\'s Fund, established by GA Resolution 57 (I) and 48/162</li>\n<li>Executive Board of the United Nations Development Programme and of the United Nations Population Fund, established by GA Resolution 2029 (XX) and 48/162</li>\n<li>Executive Board of the World Food Programme, established by GA Resolution 50/8</li></ol>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Boards_2">Boards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Boards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ol><li>Board of Auditors, established by GA Resolution 74 (I)</li>\n<li>Trade and Development Board, established by GA Resolution 1995 (XIX)</li>\n<li>United Nations Joint Staff Pension Board, established by GA Resolution 248 (III)</li>\n<li>Advisory Board on Disarmament Matters, established by GA Resolution 37/99 K</li></ol>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Councils_and_panels">Councils and panels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Councils and panels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The newest council is the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">United Nations Human Rights Council</a>, which replaced the aforementioned UNCHR in March 2006.\n</p><p>There are a total of four councils and one panel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Working_Groups_and_other">Working Groups and other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Working Groups and other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There is a varied group of working groups and other subsidiary bodies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seating">Seating</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Seating">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Countries are seated alphabetically in the General Assembly according to English translations of the countries\' names. The country which occupies the front-most left position is determined annually by the Secretary-General via ballot draw. The remaining countries follow alphabetically after it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reform_and_UNPA">Reform and UNPA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Reform and UNPA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Reform_of_the_United_Nations" title="Reform of the United Nations">Reform of the United Nations</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Parliamentary_Assembly" title="United Nations Parliamentary Assembly">United Nations Parliamentary Assembly</a></div>\n<p>On 21 March 2005, <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General</a> <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a> presented a report, <i>In Larger Freedom</i>, that criticized the General Assembly for focusing so much on consensus that it was passing watered-down resolutions reflecting "the lowest common denominator of widely different opinions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> He also criticized the Assembly for trying to address too broad an agenda, instead of focusing on "the major substantive issues of the day, such as international <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">migration</a> and the long-debated comprehensive convention on terrorism". Annan recommended streamlining the General Assembly\'s agenda, committee structure, and procedures; strengthening the role and authority of its <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="President of the United Nations General Assembly">president</a>; enhancing the role of <a href="/wiki/Civil_society" title="Civil society">civil society</a>; and establishing a mechanism to review the decisions of its committees, in order to minimize <a href="/wiki/Unfunded_mandate" title="Unfunded mandate">unfunded mandates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Micromanagement" title="Micromanagement">micromanagement</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretariat" title="United Nations Secretariat">United Nations Secretariat</a>. Annan reminded UN members of their responsibility to implement reforms, if they expect to realize improvements in UN effectiveness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The reform proposals were not taken up by the United Nations World Summit in September 2005. Instead, the Summit solely affirmed the central position of the General Assembly as the chief deliberative, policymaking and representative organ of the United Nations, as well as the advisory role of the Assembly in the process of standard-setting and the codification of international law. The Summit also called for strengthening the relationship between the General Assembly and the other principal organs to ensure better coordination on topical issues that required coordinated action by the United Nations, in accordance with their respective mandates.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>A United Nations Parliamentary Assembly, or United Nations People\'s Assembly (UNPA), is a proposed addition to the United Nations System that eventually could allow for direct election of UN parliament members by citizens all over the world.\n</p><p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_debate_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="General debate of the United Nations General Assembly">General Debate</a> of the 65th General Assembly, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Valero" title="Jorge Valero">Jorge Valero</a>, representing <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, said "The United Nations has exhausted its model and it is not simply a matter of proceeding with reform, the twenty-first century demands deep changes that are only possible with a rebuilding of this organisation." He pointed to the futility of resolutions concerning the <a href="/wiki/United_States_embargo_against_Cuba" title="United States embargo against Cuba">Cuban embargo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_modern_conflicts_in_the_Middle_East" title="List of modern conflicts in the Middle East">Middle East conflict</a> as reasons for the UN model having failed. Venezuela also called for the suspension of veto rights in the Security Council because it was a "remnant of the Second World War [it] is incompatible with the principle of sovereign equality of States".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Reform of the United Nations General Assembly includes proposals to change the powers and composition of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.N._General_Assembly" title="U.N. General Assembly">U.N. General Assembly</a>. This could include, for example, tasking the Assembly with evaluating how well member states implement UNGA resolutions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> increasing the power of the assembly vis-&#224;-vis the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>, or making debates more constructive and less repetitive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sidelines_of_the_General_Assembly">Sidelines of the General Assembly</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sidelines of the General Assembly">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The annual session of the United Nations General Assembly is accompanied by independent meetings between world leaders, better known as meetings taking place on the <i>sidelines</i> of the Assembly meeting. The diplomatic congregation has also since evolved into a week attracting wealthy and influential individuals from around the world to New York City to address various agendas, ranging from humanitarian and environmental to business and political.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYCGlobalMeeting_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYCGlobalMeeting-44">[44]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_Nations" title="History of the United Nations">History of the United Nations</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_current_Permanent_Representatives_to_the_United_Nations" title="List of current Permanent Representatives to the United Nations">List of current Permanent Representatives to the United Nations</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Reform_of_the_United_Nations" title="Reform of the United Nations">Reform of the United Nations</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Interpretation_Service" title="United Nations Interpretation Service">United Nations Interpretation Service</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_System" title="United Nations System">United Nations System</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_General_Assembly&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; United Nations.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="https://www.un.org/ga/subsidiary/" rel="nofollow">General Assembly: Subsidiary organs</a> at UN.org.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">United Nations Official Document. <a class="external text" href="http://www.un.org/ga/search/view_doc.asp?symbol=A/INF/70/1" rel="nofollow">"The annual session convenes on Tuesday of the third week in September per Resolution 57/301, Para. 1.
